  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_1e2bd6d8-aef2-4094-af52-a6868a28956f'
      });

<span class='communityAnswererName'>

<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">I really think that's a good idea to make a movie for Fablehaven...BUT! the thing that sets Fablehaven apart from Harry Potter is that you have to use<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">I really think that's a good idea to make a movie for Fablehaven...BUT! the thing that sets Fablehaven apart from Harry Potter is that you have to use your imagination! In Harry Potter you can just imagine a part from the movie when reading them. But in Fablehaven you have to imagine it. I mean, which is better the Harry Potter movies or books!? In my opinion, the books. I mean, have you seen the Percy Jackson movies! They're terrible! The books are always better than the movies.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer79764052" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4509373784726941606">For the record, I'm the publisher. Yes, I've read it. Sorry, I won't be giving anything away. Well, maybe a little something. Chapter 5 in book 5 is the most intense, the most gripping chapter of all the Fablehaven books. Jaw-dropping. I was not prepared for what Brandon Mull pulled out of his sleeve. I doubt anyone will see this coming. <br/><br/>Brandon takes us all over the world, several continents. It's a breathless race to find the remaining artifacts. The artifact vault in Austrailia is a wicked ri</span>
  <span id="freeText4509373784726941606" style="display:none">For the record, I'm the publisher. Yes, I've read it. Sorry, I won't be giving anything away. Well, maybe a little something. Chapter 5 in book 5 is the most intense, the most gripping chapter of all the Fablehaven books. Jaw-dropping. I was not prepared for what Brandon Mull pulled out of his sleeve. I doubt anyone will see this coming. <br /><br />Brandon takes us all over the world, several continents. It's a breathless race to find the remaining artifacts. The artifact vault in Austrailia is a wicked ride. The Society of the Evening Star seems unbeatable. The Sphinx's history is revealed!<br /><br />My favorite characters are Seth and Vanessa. I wish I could tell you what Vanessa knows. The truth is some secrets really are worth keeping.<br /><br />March 23, 2010. And if you're in Salt Lake City on March 23 you won't want to miss the release party. We'll announce all the details at Fablehaven.com and BrandonMull.com. <br /><br />Drink the Milk! </span>
  <a data-text-id="4509373784726941606" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText17556545099525695963" style="display:none">I had to stay up until 4 A.M. it was way too exciting to put it down. I even loved the end of the book, end of the series. I didn't think "thank heaven's it's over," like I have with others. Their was a lot of comic relief. <br /><br /><br />At the every end of the book, Brandon mentions that he might do more with the characters, but it will be with a complete different series. <div id="review_105822032" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/105822032" />
    <a title="Angie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2687901-angie"><img alt="Angie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1459874153p2/2687901.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/105822032?book_show_action=true">Jun 05, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Angie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Angie" href="/user/show/2687901-angie">Angie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Anyone</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2687901-angie?shelf=middle-grade">middle-grade</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2687901-angie?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2687901-angie?shelf=thought-stimulators">thought-stimulators</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer105822032&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer105822032" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3717398338259099838">I feel like the last few weeks of my life have been consumed by the Fablehaven series. I get home from work, play with my family, and then I finally get to dedicate a short amount of time to reading. One of the greatest things about summer is that you can read fun books that don't make you think, and Fablehaven gave me the diversion I needed. As I reached the last 20 or so pages of the series, I found myself reading slower, not wanting the ride to end. It was a good ride, but like all good thing</span>
  <span id="freeText3717398338259099838" style="display:none">I feel like the last few weeks of my life have been consumed by the Fablehaven series. I get home from work, play with my family, and then I finally get to dedicate a short amount of time to reading. One of the greatest things about summer is that you can read fun books that don't make you think, and Fablehaven gave me the diversion I needed. As I reached the last 20 or so pages of the series, I found myself reading slower, not wanting the ride to end. It was a good ride, but like all good things, the ride must end at some point. (However, there is no rule that says you can't go on the ride more than once.)<br /><br />Usually, I get annoyed by happily-ever-after endings. My English major training has done that to me. The only exception I have been able to make is Harry Potter. The Harry Potter books are perfect in every way and the characters paid a steep price to get their happy ending. I didn't feel that the Fablehaven characters paid that steep of a price to get their happy ending; however, the ending didn't annoy me--it was actually quite satisfying. I find myself comparing the book to the battles that we all must face while here in mortality. The fight seems hopeless at times, but there is always a ray of hope that things will be better--eternally better. I think the most strong parallel of this is seen in the Fairy Queen giving up her realm for the good of all of mankind. That was the biggest sacrifice she could have made, and yet, she was rewarded a hundredfold in the end. She got to build up bigger and better kingdom, and this time she had her husband and her son by her side. I am a firm believer that if we are willing to sacrifice now, we will be rewarded an uncountable amount of time in the future. All we have to do is play our part, and we will experience eternal joy in the end.<br /><br />I really enjoyed the role Doren and Newel played in these books. And Hugo. Hugo has become one of my most favorite characters. He is kind of synonomous with Hurley from Lost. Seth no longer drives me crazy--in fact, his sense of humor had me laughing out loud many times, something that usually only happens when I am reading Harry Potter. I am glad that Warren was able to play such a big part in the books. He is probably my most favorite character. However, I am still not a huge fan of Kendra. Despite the amazing things she has done, she still seems like a little girl to me, a little girl that is too afraid to jump off the high dive. That made the whole romance with Bracken even weirder. I must admit, I didn't see that coming. But alas, romance abounds everywhere. Bracken and Kendra's romance weirded me out less than the whole Warren and Vanessa thing. But maybe that is just because I wanted Warren to myself.<br /><br />Now the books have come to an end, and it is time for me to start thinking about a new series to keep me occupied. However, whenever I think back on Doren and Newel's fondness for television, on Seth's and Warren's boyish fantasies, on the magical beauty of Fablehaven, I don't think I'll be able to stop the smile. Even in the world that I live in, Fablehaven can still work its magic.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3717398338259099838" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

And whether or not it was intentional, Raxtus made me laugh. It's interesting to see Kendra's relationship with the Fairy Queen develop. I'm glad Seth's character is growing up; he's a lot like Warren now. Unfortunately, Warren has the worst luck of anyone.</span>

  <span id="freeText2149047111029479350" style="display:none">The conclusion to the five book series focusing on a brother and sister who discover a magical world run by their grandparents. I'm in the minority for loving it way more than Harry Schmotter, er, Potter. :) <br /><br />Anyway, without giving spoilers there are a good number of twists and minor to moderate surprises. Mind you, that's for an adult reading the book. I suspect teen agers might be more amazed by things and such. Bracken was the most interesting secondary character and the verbal duels with the Sphinx as well as the many fairy preserves were thought provoking. <br /><br /><b>PAGE COUNT: 544 pp.; WHEN READ: March to July 2010; MY GRADE: B to B plus.</b></span>

<div id="review_346149802" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/346149802" />
    <a title="Turtle" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10129675-turtle"><img alt="Turtle" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1379663725p2/10129675.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/346149802?book_show_action=true">Jun 10, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Turtle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Turtle" href="/user/show/10129675-turtle">Turtle</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">I would not recommend this book</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Turtle by: </span>
      My Uncle
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10129675-turtle?shelf=wish-i-never-read">wish-i-never-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10129675-turtle?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10129675-turtle?shelf=apocalyptic">apocalyptic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10129675-turtle?shelf=children-s">children-s</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer346149802&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer346149802" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer381882530736552357">Ugh. Where to start with this one? <br/><br/>It wasn't as hard to read as Breaking Dawn. But it wasn't easy. Most of the time I would be in the middle of reading the book... wishing I was doing something else. That's never a good sign by the way. You don't want your readers to be wishing they were not reading your story. <br/><br/>This book had a major strike against it. I just didn't give a crap anymore. All these bad things are happening to the characters, but I really couldn't care less. <br/><br/>Seth gets kidnapped... b</span>
  <span id="freeText381882530736552357" style="display:none">Ugh. Where to start with this one? <br /><br />It wasn't as hard to read as Breaking Dawn. But it wasn't easy. Most of the time I would be in the middle of reading the book... wishing I was doing something else. That's never a good sign by the way. You don't want your readers to be wishing they were not reading your story. <br /><br />This book had a major strike against it. I just didn't give a crap anymore. All these bad things are happening to the characters, but I really couldn't care less. <br /><br />Seth gets kidnapped... but I don't remember how. Oh right. They were trying to go through another secret preserve. Yawn. I think the major problem with this book was that Mull was trying to make you feel how terrible the bad guys are, how terrifying, how threatening by killing off character that we don't care about at all. Mull even goes as far as to introduce these Eternals who are immortals that must die before the demon prison can be opened. Kendra and the gang rushes to stop these Eternals from dying without knowing that the readers don't really care... at all. In fact we're hoping that she won't rescue them so that something exciting might happen. The game of cat and mouse gets real dull after awhile. <br /><br />In fact, you need these Eternals to die to get a move on with the plot. So why bother even introducing us to them? Why bother taking up valuable chapter space to introduce the Eternal to us, attempt to make us sympathize with him, when you know and I know that the Eternal must die. A much more effect way to handle the Eternals is just to make Kendra and the gang always too late. Or maybe they come just in time to watch one of the Eternals die. The last one, we can get to meet, feel bad for her, and then you can kill her. That death would be more meaningful. She was the last one, the last hope. We meet her, get to know her- and the readers generally want to save her. You'll even trick them into thinking "Oh! She's still alive! They've got time! They might win this!" THEN YOU KILL HER! That will create natural tension. It would make the readers actually mourn her loss, even if we never got a chance to really know her. <br /><br />In all honesty, I wouldn't have included the stupid plot device in the first place. <br /><br />So two new characters get introduced in this book. Nagi Luna, an evil demon witch mastermind which I guess is supposed to mirror the evil witch with the knots from the first story. And Gavin 2.0. No, his name isn't Gavin. But really that's all he appeared to be. His real name is Bracken... (I like Gavin 2.0 better) and he's a unicorn. Meaning he's Kendra's new love buddy. I kind of saw him as Mull's way of apologizing to all those Gavin fans who were upset when Gavin turned out to be evil (rather randomly I might add) in the last book. He's a unicorn, Kendra! So it's safe for you to fall hopelessly in love with him! <br /><br />Anyway, stuff happens. Kendra's leads a rescue mission to save Seth. Which fails. Then Kendra leads a rescue mission to save the Eternals which also fails. I mean so far, the book's looking great! <br /><br />Seth rescues himself and goes on an epic quest involving Patton, creepy fate witches and a sword. I mean, his whole half of the story starts with him being skewered, imprisoned, and then coming back to Fablehaven to... accidently let loose a demon a hundred times worse than the bad guy they were already fighting.<br /><br />Way to go Seth. Way to fall into the most obvious trap ever. <br /><br />I'm sorry Seth. I don't hate you. It's not your fault that your author doesn't take you seriously. <br /><br />Anyway so Seth ends up accidently killing one of his friends. Which is... semi touching. I actually thought Coulter's sacrifice in the second book was much more noble and touching. Really if Mull put the same emotion behind that scene into this one, it might have made me sad... maybe. Anyway, so his friend dies, and yet again I'm not really sad about it. Seth goes on a quest to make things right. <br /><br />And already it's more interesting than whatever Kendra's doing. After all Seth's team consists of Vanessa (who I always thought was pretty awesome) and the satyrs (who I automatically liked because their grandpa didn't like them). I mean already you have the makings for a more interesting adventure. And for the most part it is. And a more fruitful one at that. Seth's actions very well saved all their lives. <br /><br />But then, of course, Mull has to take it all away. Because of course, Seth can't possibly save the day can he? Only Kendra has that deus ex machina power. Even if it would make more sense that Seth be the hero. Kendra has to yank the spot light away... again. <br /><br />So we get to the island the prison is on. And all the characters are moaning about how they're all about to die. And I say "No such luck, guys! I wouldn't get that lucky!" Then Mr. Gavin 2.0- Unicorn guy pipes up and says "Hey! We might not have to die after all! I have a vague plan up my sleeve! Just trust me!" And in all honesty, the way the pull the whole stupid thing off isn't important. In fact, it was the most stupidly obvious plan I'm kind of annoyed that I didn't see it coming. Not as bad as the first book but still...<br /><br />What is important is that Seth gets a whole chapter to be a hero. And in that chapter he takes out not one but two really powerful demons. With the awesome sword that he collected on his quest, I might add. The task of defeating these demons very nearly kills him, but it still was a pretty sweet moment. <br /><br />And just when I have the smallest... oh who am I kidding. I was pretty sure at the end of that chapter, Mull was going to piss me off again. <br /><br />So Seth comes back to the sidelines all beaten up. And Kendra, seeing her brother in this state, is really upset. She picks up his sword and... turns super sayian. <br /><br />Now to understand why I hate this part of the book you have to understand something about this sword. Seth went on a half a book long quest to get this sword. His blood sweat and tears are in it now. And not only did he have to go kill people for the sword, it chose him as its new owner. The first new owner in over a century. Seth was supposed to be seen as this remarkable human being for having accomplished such a feat. It was his one true outshining of his sister. It may not have been as pretty a accomplishment as her "fairy born" crap was. But it was something he worked hard for. He earned that sword. <br /><br />Kendra picks it up after it "calls to her" and freaking turns into a super fairy chick. She goes all berserker on the biggest and baddest king of demons and manages to KILL him WITHOUT a single scratch. You can't say this wouldn't sicken you. I mean it sickens me just typing this. <br /><br />Might I also add that both the Fairy Queen herself and her son (Gavin 2.0) were fighting the demon without so much as scratching him. And little Kendra comes out of nowhere and hacks him to pieces. This should piss every reader off. Obviously it didn't, because people put this book on the New York Times Best Sellers list. <br /><br />How Seth must have felt when his sister picked up "his" sword! He kind of laughs it off but you can tell through Seth's body language and dialogue (even if Mull didn't mean it) that Seth is not thrilled with his sister's success. I may be reading into something that isn't there. But when Seth started downplaying his own role in their victory when explaining to his parents and praising Kendra's- I just wanted to give him a hug. Wouldn't you feel like crap if that happened to you? I mean, sure you'd be happy to be alive. And you'd be glad that the demon king was defeated. But wouldn't you feel like all your hard work was just to be a messenger boy for your elder sister? Talk about incoming inferiority complex. <br /><br />Mull even writes in something along the lines of "Seth wasn't even upset that Kendra defeated the demon king singlehandedly..." in exposition. But really, that was more like Mull trying to cover up his mistake. He knew Seth would be pissed. But instead of writing his character like his character were a real person, he pretends that Seth is okay with the whole thing. So that in the final scenes, Seth seems real distant and out of character. <br /><br />I think Mull just realized that he was almost done with this stupid series and just couldn't stand to write anymore. So he didn't put any serious thought into how Seth might have felt. And instead focused on the Gavin 2.0 and Kendra love story. Which is really not that cute. Most of the time I was just like... oh just kiss her and go away already. I'm tired of both of you. <br /><br />Seth was supposed to have a minor quest at the end. Something he promised the fates. But Mull didn't think it was important to follow up on it because it would mean Seth would get to do something awesome and Mull hates Seth. <br /><br />So he ends the series with Kendra sharing a tender moment with unicorn boy. And Seth kinda off to the side, wondering when he will get his own book series.</span>
  <a data-text-id="381882530736552357" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_97593536" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/97593536" />
    <a title="Emily Michelle" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1729215-emily-michelle"><img alt="Emily Michelle" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1229045392p2/1729215.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/97593536?book_show_action=true">Apr 08, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily Michelle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily Michelle" href="/user/show/1729215-emily-michelle">Emily Michelle</a>
      </span>

        rated it

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer97593536" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14740466508990802126">I started this book a few evenings after it came out and told myself I would put it down and go to bed as soon as I reached a stopping point. I finished the book seven hours later, having read the entire thing straight through, because as it turned out, there are no stopping points. The book sucks you in from the first chapter and doesn't let you go until it's done.<br/><br/>The story follows Kendra, Seth and their friends all over the world, from the Middle East to the American deep south to Scotland to </span>
  <span id="freeText14740466508990802126" style="display:none">I started this book a few evenings after it came out and told myself I would put it down and go to bed as soon as I reached a stopping point. I finished the book seven hours later, having read the entire thing straight through, because as it turned out, there are no stopping points. The book sucks you in from the first chapter and doesn't let you go until it's done.<br /><br />The story follows Kendra, Seth and their friends all over the world, from the Middle East to the American deep south to Scotland to the Canadian wilderness. There they encounter Mull's usual array of original magical beings and familiar mythical creatures with the author's unique twist. Kendra and Seth both grow immensely in this book, with Kendra learning that sometimes you have to take action and Seth learning that sometimes you have to think. Reading the last battle scene, it's really incredible to see how far they've come, when you think of how in the first book, Kendra was shy and scared and Seth was pretty much an idiot.<br /><br />And the book is surprisingly profound in places, commenting, without preaching, about the nature of good and evil and temptation and choices. A great read and an excellent end to an excellent series.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14740466508990802126" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_203589175" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/203589175" />
    <a title="Samuel Loveland" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5033995-samuel-loveland"><img alt="Samuel Loveland" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1314727439p2/5033995.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/203589175?book_show_action=true">Aug 30, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Samuel Loveland" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Samuel Loveland" href="/user/show/5033995-samuel-loveland">Samuel Loveland</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer203589175" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2450181722925991492">There seems to be a generation of Harry Potter fans who are looking for the fun, adventure, and growth that we experienced in that series. When cop-outs like Percy Jackson came out, we snatched them up in order to quench our thirst for more. What we got from these wanna-be stories is a sense of fun and adventure, but a lack of something deeper.<br/><br/>Don’t get me wrong. I both read and enjoyed the Percy Jackson books. They were adventurous and a whole lot of fun. However, I think most people would agre</span>
  <span id="freeText2450181722925991492" style="display:none">There seems to be a generation of Harry Potter fans who are looking for the fun, adventure, and growth that we experienced in that series. When cop-outs like Percy Jackson came out, we snatched them up in order to quench our thirst for more. What we got from these wanna-be stories is a sense of fun and adventure, but a lack of something deeper.<br /><br />Don’t get me wrong. I both read and enjoyed the Percy Jackson books. They were adventurous and a whole lot of fun. However, I think most people would agree with my assessment that held up to Harry Potter, it was missing something.<br /><br />Fablehaven is no cop-out. It’s a fantastic story that bows to no cliche’s without stretching them. It is a story about kids thrown into a world of magic, kids that still have families. (I know right? For awhile there we began to think that kids HAD to be orphans in order to have adventures.) It has the fun. It has the family-friendly appropriateness for all ages. It has the depth of character and theme. One of the strongest themes of the series is in the different types of heroism displayed by the two main characters.<br /><br />Kendra vs. Seth<br /><br />Kendra appeals to the sense that purity wins. She has her stuff together, she thinks things through, and she follows the rules (unless it would be more prudent not to). Throughout the series, this attribute, combined with her pure intentions, have won the day several times over.<br /><br />Seth, on the other hand, is headstrong, rambunctious, and a little bit of a troublemaker – a man after my heart. In another world, he might have been named Calvin. Seth is consistently breaking rules, with the best of intentions, and making a mess of things. His mistakes needlessly throw others into danger, and though Seth does care, he doesn’t ever seem to gain his sister’s cool head.<br /><br />Both are heroes. We have the pure hero, and the one who screwed up and has to fix it. Thematically, we have two lessons; first, that it is better not to screw up in the first place and second, that if you’ve already screwed up, you can learn from this by doing what you can to make it better.<br /><br />But theme isn’t the only thing the book has going for it. With a world full of fairies, demons, Eternals, powerful artifacts and satyrs who are addicted to TV and junk food… well, to quote a certain Star Trek character,<br /><br />“You don’t have to take my word for it”<br /><br />Go pick one up for yourself. Or better yet, for us students, borrow from a friend – this is a series worth discussing with buddies.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="2450181722925991492" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1134476145" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1134476145" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17232845466641724896"><b>{December 19th, 2014} MINI-REVIEW</b><br/><br/>4 to 4.5 stars, I want MOAR.<br/><br/><b>
  <i>“Try as we might to postpone them, days of reckoning inevitably arrive.”</i>
</b><br/><br/>Well this was certainly quite the ride. Everything really managed to be covered in almost 600 pages and in a smooth way to almost. I'm surprised how much work went into this final book. After the last book, I was wondering how it would hold up. Thankfully I was surprised again, especially since I finished this within less a day. Pretty insane, huh?<br/><br/>Now what to s</span>
  <span id="freeText17232845466641724896" style="display:none"><b>{December 19th, 2014} MINI-REVIEW</b><br /><br />4 to 4.5 stars, I want MOAR.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>“Try as we might to postpone them, days of reckoning inevitably arrive.”</i>
</b><br /><br />Well this was certainly quite the ride. Everything really managed to be covered in almost 600 pages and in a smooth way to almost. I'm surprised how much work went into this final book. After the last book, I was wondering how it would hold up. Thankfully I was surprised again, especially since I finished this within less a day. Pretty insane, huh?<br /><br />Now what to say about this final installment that probably hasn't been said?<br /><br />The final chapter was a troll ending response from the author, had me going NOOO I WANT MOAR FABLEHAVEN though lmao. But that's the thing about good series, you're supposed feel that way by the end. I'm glad I stuck with this series despite my first thoughts and impressions.<br /><br />I do hope Mull returns to this world in some form, it really is sound and magical.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>“Some imagine the difference between heaven and hell to be a matter of geography. Not so. The difference is much more evident in the individuals who dwell there.”</i>
</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="17232845466641724896" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_96363513" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/96363513" />
    <a title="Fraffee" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3514917-fraffee"><img alt="Fraffee" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1468797164p2/3514917.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/96363513?book_show_action=true">Mar 30, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Fraffee" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Fraffee" href="/user/show/3514917-fraffee">Fraffee</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Harry Potter Fans, Percy Jackson Fans, Lovers of fantasy and mythology, Kids at heart</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3514917-fraffee?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer96363513&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer96363513" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6728534692574679697">WOAH. <br/>Yup, my first attempt at writing an intellectual review begins with the word, WOAH.<br/>I've been loyal to the Fablehaven series ever since I read the first book. I instantly fell in love with the ideas that were found in Brandon Mull's books. I've been waiting for a series like this, practically all my life - not kidding. Now that it is ending, I feel like I just passed through to a new stage of my childhood. That is why I feel so pressured in giving this final book the best review I could eve</span>
  <span id="freeText6728534692574679697" style="display:none">WOAH. <br />Yup, my first attempt at writing an intellectual review begins with the word, WOAH.<br />I've been loyal to the Fablehaven series ever since I read the first book. I instantly fell in love with the ideas that were found in Brandon Mull's books. I've been waiting for a series like this, practically all my life - not kidding. Now that it is ending, I feel like I just passed through to a new stage of my childhood. That is why I feel so pressured in giving this final book the best review I could ever 'try' to write. <br /><br />My first thoughts were, again, WOAH. I was instantly hooked from the start of Chapter 1 to the end of Chapter 30. I nearly sobbed when I read Kendra's last words because it meant that the series was over. But really, the last book was the perfect icing on Bradon Mull's ever so complicated yet brilliantly baked fantasy cake. <br /><br />I don't actually know where to begin. But I guess I should start praising the characters since they were the ones that kept the story going. I would like to hail Seth as one of my favorite characters in the series; but my liking for him grew in the last book. Yeah, he's messed up more than any other character in the books but what I love about Seth is his desire to make things right. I was rooting for him, cheering him on all the way. I find him very endearing and that's what makes me love him even more. Besides his courage and his desire for justice, I found him also to be very protective. He loves his family and will stop at nothing to save them - as seen in his quest for Vasilis. I would also like to note his compassion in helping Graulas. I knew the monster was no spongecake softy but I don't hate Seth for healing him. It just shows he's a good person, willing to help others even if it's beyond his abilities. He really matured over the last few books - but as seen by the television-generator bargains, Seth will always be Seth, and that's fine with me. Moving on, to other characters I liked - Kendra, Bracken, and Warren. Kendra, too good to be true obedient daughter or not, I love her anyways. She's just as endearing as her brother. Many may argue her to be boring and bland but I think she had a spunk to her in this book. I found her little fling with Bracken adorable. It really didn't feel weird to me because they'd be the perfect match - fairykind maiden and a unicorn fairy prince, best combination ever. By the way, I literally got chills when Bracken gave his speech before battle in Shoreless Isle. His bravery made me love him as well. Also, I'd have to commend Warren for his outstanding loyalty. He stuck with the Sorenson clan through thick and thin - mostly thick. He's the older version of Seth, I think that's why he grew on me. Now in the magical aspect, I would say that I loved Hugo the most. My heart ached when his ached - weird, but I felt him to be more human than some of the 'real' human characters in the book. His bond with Seth is too cute. Raxtus really blew me away in this book. He is literally the coolest dragon ever. And oh please don't get me started on Coulter. I'll just burst into tears again because I really was fond of him. His death really tugged at my heartstrings. He may seem like a hard egg but he has grown on me because I see him in a grandfatherly way. <br /><br />Now, onto the plot - which was amazing, just so you know. It had all the things I was craving for. Crazy battle scenes, mythical creatures, a narrative filled with suspense, funny conversations, and more - much more. I can tell that Brandon Mull really gave his all when he wrote this because it was an explosion of WONDER - the preserve in Australia alone already got me dancing in my room. The book was pure epic magic. Each chapter was filled with so much that I was afraid I wasn't going to remember any of the details but then again, Mr. Mull has a way of keeping one up to speed on events. His writing was really easy and fluid. But there were times when I kinda felt weary from his overly detailed descriptions. Actually, I sometimes love the overly detailed stuff because I get to visualize them in my head. Even with this little 'thing', HIS WRITING IS STILL WICKED.I don't think I'll ever find another author who can cook something as insane as this series and write it in a way that would give it justice. <br /><br />The ending was pretty perfect in my opinion. Was it predictable? At one point yes, and the rest, well I was completed taken aback by some of the events because I never expected them. Brandon Mull is so brilliant - his idea of using the Fairy Realm to serve as the new prison is genius. I found the fight scenes glorious and Lord of the Rings-esque but during the battle with the demon horde, I was kinda expecting more. But in the end, Mull made everything better with his clever dialogue and his magical way with words. As a 300/LOTR type of person, I was really satisfied by all the fighting scenes Mull presented. Some were somewhat literally unbelievable but I loved it anyway - cause, hey, it's a fantasy novel. One thing just bugged me - everything worked out so easily for Kendra and Seth. But I was truly still satisfied by the outcome of everything. I also have to consider the fact that Kendra and Seth are not ordinary kids. They both have an endearing spirit. That spirit - the desire to help their friends, the desire to free their families and the deep longing to save the world despite the chances of death being nearly a 100 percent - propelled them and enabled them to do the crazy things that they did. Seth killing Nagi Luna and Graulus was no small feet but in a way believable because his extreme love for everyone else made his victory possible. When Kendra defeated Gorgrog, I then thought that people would go through extra lengths to protect their loved ones. The forces of light also overpowered the darkness because of the extreme desire to restore what's right. <br /><br />Besides bravery, loyalty, perseverance and hopefulness, the last concluding lesson I learned from this series is that ordinary people can do extraordinary things. Two simple kids who just wanted everything to be right - ended up restoring what is right and more. Brandon Mull is an inspiration, all writers should be more like him. <br /><br />Getting teary eyed is unavoidable. I'm sad that this series is over but at least I'm at peace with what Brandon Mull has written. He tied everything together perfectly - just like a beautiful ribbon decoration on a present. And it got me thinking, this book is probably one of the greatest contributions to the Young Adult Fantasy genre - a true 'present' indeed. </span>
  <a data-text-id="6728534692574679697" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer18169545741265545483">Beotch... wut. The conclusion to this series was really good, but I'm happy I finally finished them. <br/>I was so happy when Kendra liked Bracken, and he returned her affection, I was so ecstatic. I ship them so hard. I mean, I don't really think that Kendra can be with anyone else.   <span id="freeText18169545741265545483" style="display:none">Beotch... wut. The conclusion to this series was really good, but I'm happy I finally finished them. <br />I was so happy when Kendra liked Bracken, and he returned her affection, I was so ecstatic. I ship them so hard. I mean, I don't really think that Kendra can be with anyone else. The concept of her being an Eternal was cool, but I was really wondering, since she is fairykind, wouldn't she be virtually immortal?? <br />The death of Coulter didn't really bother me, since he was in reality a minor player. Also Vanessa wasn't actually bad, so that was really good. <br />When it was revealed the the Larson grandparents were alive and well, it didn't really affect me, I mean, they were assumed dead from book one, why should I care about them now? <br />I know that there isn't supposed to be a continuation of this series. But I am still hoping for a new series that revisits this magical world. The magic creatures were really cool, and I would like to see more of those in the books (if there is ever a continuation). <br />5/5 stars, I was satisfied with the ending provided.</span>

<div id="review_2328584764" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2328584764" />
    <a title="Mercy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12155957-mercy"><img alt="Mercy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1516580041p2/12155957.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

<span id="freeTextContainer6095549850368117400">I'm done! It was tough getting through 2,412 pages of a series in a short period of time, but the Fablehaven series was a really solid read. Keys to the Demon Prison is my son's favorite book of all time now. What a successful ending! Kendra and Seth are so grown up, and I may have gotten a little teary at their parents at the end of this one.<br/><br/>There is a sequel series (<a href='https://www.goodreads.com/series/199517-dragonwatch' rel='nofollow noopener'>Dragonwatch</a>). My son has already flown through the first two and is finishing up the third one that was just released this month. I'm choosing to sit that one out, but he's loving it. If you enjoy middle grade fantasy, definitely give this one a chance. Otherwise, gift it to an up and coming reader in your life.</span>

<div id="review_140315728" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/140315728" />
    <a title="Ithlilian" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4793655-ithlilian"><img alt="Ithlilian" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1392859819p2/4793655.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/140315728?book_show_action=true">Jan 12, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ithlilian" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ithlilian" href="/user/show/4793655-ithlilian">Ithlilian</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4793655-ithlilian?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer140315728" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9330823575673376393">Keys to the Demon Prison is full of action, but that is about all there is to it. The book picks up right in the midst of things and never lets up. I personally didn't enjoy it. There are about 20 tasks that need to be completed and the characters systematically go through them. Traveling to each event takes 20 or so pages, the actual event takes a page, and then it is on to the next thing. There is no flow here, and no elegance. I loved the whimsical nature of the first Fablehaven book. It's a </span>
  <span id="freeText9330823575673376393" style="display:none">Keys to the Demon Prison is full of action, but that is about all there is to it. The book picks up right in the midst of things and never lets up. I personally didn't enjoy it. There are about 20 tasks that need to be completed and the characters systematically go through them. Traveling to each event takes 20 or so pages, the actual event takes a page, and then it is on to the next thing. There is no flow here, and no elegance. I loved the whimsical nature of the first Fablehaven book. It's a book that really made me want to live the lives of the characters. What could be more fun and interesting than exploring a place full of mystical creatures and uncovering secrets? Now these books feel like chores, as if each character is presented with a list of things to do, and they go do them. It is just not enough. I really didn't care what person or place was coming up next. In fact, throughout this entire book all I wanted was for it to be over. I felt the same way about the last Percy Jackson book. Running around from place to place does not make an interesting novel. It's extremely repetitious and boring, no matter how much action you want to throw in there. The characters don't help the book much either. The book is so focused on events that the characters feel like bystanders. You could insert any character in the novel and they would do just fine. The personalities aren't really as present in this book as in others, and no one has matured or changed much from book one. Throwing in many additional characters in each book does not help improve the series, it just adds to the short choppy nature of each book. Each character gets a few sentences of explanation, then off they go to complete their tasks. The only interesting part of this book was the beginning. I did enjoy exploring the first dungeon, but once I realized that running through dangerous areas was all the book was about, my interest took a nose dive. Keys to the Demon Prison felt more like a video game than an exciting novel with specific tasks to complete, objects to retrieve and places to go. Fans of the series should read it for closure alone, but I was very disappointed and struggled to finish it. </span>
  <a data-text-id="9330823575673376393" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_96638872" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/96638872" />
    <a title="Amanda" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1730838-amanda"><img alt="Amanda" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1430319998p2/1730838.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/96638872?book_show_action=true">Apr 01, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Amanda" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Amanda" href="/user/show/1730838-amanda">Amanda</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer96638872" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1590265687776998257">My issue with this book is the same issue I've had with all of Mull's other books. The execution of his ideas is just mediocre. From a technical/grammatical standpoint, it's written pretty poorly. He employs very little imagery, and sometimes sounds like he learned to write by reading too many fantasy novels. Most good writers will show me what is happening. Mull just tells me. Lengthy descriptions and big words don't necessarily make good writing. <br/><br/>He took a long time to get into the flow of thi</span>
  <span id="freeText1590265687776998257" style="display:none">My issue with this book is the same issue I've had with all of Mull's other books. The execution of his ideas is just mediocre. From a technical/grammatical standpoint, it's written pretty poorly. He employs very little imagery, and sometimes sounds like he learned to write by reading too many fantasy novels. Most good writers will show me what is happening. Mull just tells me. Lengthy descriptions and big words don't necessarily make good writing. <br /><br />He took a long time to get into the flow of this book, which makes the first half seems very sporadic. I also think it was a mistake to introduce so many new characters in the last book of a series. In my mind, there were more concise ways to accomplish his goals without bringing in new people. <br /><br />His ideas are good, he's pretty creative, and his characters are well developed, so in general, I like the story. I just wish it had been better written. </span>
  <a data-text-id="1590265687776998257" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="C.P. Cabaniss" class="user" itemprop="url" name="C.P. Cabaniss" href="/user/show/9656259-c-p-cabaniss">C.P. Cabaniss</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9656259-c-p-cabaniss?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9656259-c-p-cabaniss?shelf=middle-grade">middle-grade</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1574882117" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6757151898183736660">I've finally completed this series and I am so glad I finally read it! It took me a long time to continue after reading the first book, but I'm so glad I finally did. <br/><br/>I won't go into too many details, since this is the final book of a series, but it wrapped things up nicely and had a satisfying conclusion. Seth and Warren are still my two favorite characters, though there aren't many that I don't like. <br/><br/>This had a lot of great battle scenes and our characters faced great challenges. A lot happens</span>
  <span id="freeText6757151898183736660" style="display:none">I've finally completed this series and I am so glad I finally read it! It took me a long time to continue after reading the first book, but I'm so glad I finally did. <br /><br />I won't go into too many details, since this is the final book of a series, but it wrapped things up nicely and had a satisfying conclusion. Seth and Warren are still my two favorite characters, though there aren't many that I don't like. <br /><br />This had a lot of great battle scenes and our characters faced great challenges. A lot happens within this nearly 600 pages installment. Some of it is heartbreaking, but there are still plenty of laughs along the way. <br /><br />I highly recommend this series. It's well written (it gets better as you go along), with a fun cast of characters, and excellent world building. </span>

<div id="review_76858860" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/76858860" />
    <a title="Erica (storybookend)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2835464-erica-storybookend"><img alt="Erica (storybookend)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1595779045p2/2835464.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/76858860?book_show_action=true">Nov 05, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Erica (storybookend)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Erica (storybookend)" href="/user/show/2835464-erica-storybookend">Erica (storybookend)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Everyone!!</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2835464-erica-storybookend?shelf=love-love-it">love-love-it</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2835464-erica-storybookend?shelf=i-own">i-own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2835464-erica-storybookend?shelf=2010-reads">2010-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2835464-erica-storybookend?shelf=absolute-favorites">absolute-favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2835464-erica-storybookend?shelf=purely-brilliant">purely-brilliant</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2835464-erica-storybookend?shelf=i-recommend-it">i-recommend-it</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2835464-erica-storybookend?shelf=best-endings">best-endings</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2835464-erica-storybookend?shelf=lds-authors">lds-authors</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2835464-erica-storybookend?shelf=2014-reads">2014-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2835464-erica-storybookend?shelf=would-love-if-it-were-a-movie">would-love-if-it-were-a-movie</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer76858860" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16126912254565009166">Can I give Fablehaven Keys to the Demon Prison ten stars? Shining with Kendra’s blinding countenance? Well, it certainly deserves it! <br/><br/>Ah, where do I begin? I. LOVE. THIS. BOOK!!! It is my new favorite book of all times. My favorite series. I just couldn’t get enough of it! I couldn’t read it fast enough. Brandon is an amazing storyteller, and was able to captivate me from the very beginning of the series. Each book got better, escalating in thrill and adventure. The last book executed the finale</span>
  <span id="freeText16126912254565009166" style="display:none">Can I give Fablehaven Keys to the Demon Prison ten stars? Shining with Kendra’s blinding countenance? Well, it certainly deserves it! <br /><br />Ah, where do I begin? I. LOVE. THIS. BOOK!!! It is my new favorite book of all times. My favorite series. I just couldn’t get enough of it! I couldn’t read it fast enough. Brandon is an amazing storyteller, and was able to captivate me from the very beginning of the series. Each book got better, escalating in thrill and adventure. The last book executed the finale perfectly. It was perfect, absolutely amazing. Brandon tied up every loose end. He wrote such superb battle scenes, and showed clearly what people are thinking. It didn’t leave me wanting in anything. I’m thrilled that it ended the way it did, with the demon prison and everything. There couldn’t have been any other way. There are not very many people who can create such a complex fantastical magical word that is so alluring and told with such finesse. <br /><br />The characters were amazing. I love Bracken! The sweet, studly hero. He’s the kind of man that I want. Newel and Doren got funnier every minute. And Mendigo! I can’t believe how much I missed him until I finished the book. And I’m so glad that Raxtus was there, and see how his story ended. Even the Sphinx’s story ended good. Although partly the bad guy, he was able to receive some justice in the end. And there were a few pleasant surprises that just added to the perfectness of this book. Oh, and the astrids. I love the astrids! So cool.<br /><br />I know Brandon said he doesn’t plan on continuing Fablehaven, but, gosh, I would love to read about Kendra and her new life that has so many bright opportunities unfolding in front of her, and to see how Seth fares in his life. Well, I guess we can’t have everything. Still, I can’t complain. I couldn’t ask for more in a book. Brilliant! Brandon said that this book would take us for a ride. Well, he didn’t disappoint. This was one heck of a rollercoaster! <br /><br />Brandon writes so descriptively. Reading Keys to the Demon Prison, I was literally on the edge of my seat, bringing the book closer and closer to my face, trying to inhale everything in one breath, all of the vivid scenes that Brandon was portraying, the emotions that the characters were feeling. The pure majestic and thrill of the adventure kept my excitement on edge, making me eager to know the end! and not leaving me disappointed in any way. Keys to the Demon Prison was an absolutely brilliant end to an amazingly intricate, breathtaking series. I would recommend this series to every single person I see. And I will guard these treasured books as much as the centaurs guard the horn of Grunhold. I don’t know how I can contain my enthusiasm for what Brandon brings next; which he says is better?! Holy Frito-Lay Brandon! Bring it on!<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="16126912254565009166" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_95604316" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/95604316" />
    <a title="Blaine" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1136904-blaine"><img alt="Blaine" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1268690405p2/1136904.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/95604316?book_show_action=true">Mar 24, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Blaine" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Blaine" href="/user/show/1136904-blaine">Blaine</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1136904-blaine?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer95604316&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer95604316" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8642095567815556782">For the most part, I really liked it. There were some really cool and exciting parts. However, I felt that this book kind of lost some of the steam that the other books had. It just didn't feel quite so engaging. I really liked the beggining, but after that, it seemed to slow down, despite that the action didn't stop. <br/>I really liked Seth's quest to get Vasilis and Kendra and Braken's journey to save the Eternals. Those were my favorite parts. It was the ending that really bugged me.<br/>For five book</span>
  <span id="freeText8642095567815556782" style="display:none">For the most part, I really liked it. There were some really cool and exciting parts. However, I felt that this book kind of lost some of the steam that the other books had. It just didn't feel quite so engaging. I really liked the beggining, but after that, it seemed to slow down, despite that the action didn't stop. <br />I really liked Seth's quest to get Vasilis and Kendra and Braken's journey to save the Eternals. Those were my favorite parts. It was the ending that really bugged me.<br />For five books, Brandon Mull has been setting us up for the final battle. We've been constantly reminded how powerful and dangerous the demons were, and how if they got out it would be the end of the world. So the battle against the demon army should have been the most climatic and epic battle ever. But it wasn't. <br />I think the biggest problem was that there wasn't enough detail. He gave a basic description of the battle, but no detail. The whole time I was wondering, "How is Bracken fighting with a horn?" "What are the fairies doing?" Etc, etc. I wanted to know HOW they were fighting. Were the fairies making magical defenses? Were they stunning demons? Turning them to stone? Blowing the up? Same thing with the unicorns and demons. <br />Without this detail, the battle felt incomplete. I tried to imagine it myself, but the battle was moving too fast for me to do it. <br />I also thought that they killed the demons too easily. Even with a legendary sword, Seth killed Graulas pretty fast. Same thing with Kendra and the Demon King. A little more struggle would have made much more excititng.<br />I also felt that the romance between Kendra and Braken too sudden. It felt like it was put there for the sake of having romance, not because it added to the story (I may be biast, since I don't like romantic books). It felt thrown onto the end, and not woven into the book. <br />Well despite all that negitivity, I stilled enjoyed the book. I just wish Brandon Mull had taken a little more time at the end, and not rushed it so much. </span>
  <a data-text-id="8642095567815556782" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('yp0vUDikIGCE1N06VPULsmIJt4gDOkmRloKzwWwsY2HRlA4QQ3YBzYGYXB5ItP2aflpA0TjzbiY/sZQgcJVO3Q==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

Baśniowego, tajemniczego i na pozór przyjaznego, choć Łukasz szybko się przekona, że tylko do czasu... „Za niebieskimi drzwiami” Marcina Szczygielskiego to – podobnie jak „Omega” i „Czarny Młyn” (ukaże się w marcu 2011 r.) tego samego autora – książka dla młodzieży. Można ją nazwać powieścią przygodową czy obyczajową, choć znajdziemy w niej też liczne motywy znane z literatury science fiction i horrorów. Niezwykle precyzyjnie jest w niej budowane napięcie – prosta na początku fabuła obfituje w nieoczekiwane zwroty, nic też nie zapowiada zaskakującego finału… Równie ważne jak pochłaniająca czytelnika akcja jest jednak to, że książka tak wyraziście mówi o emocjach współczesnych nastolatków – ich samotności, marzeniach, wyborach – oraz nieumiejętności budowania relacji zarówno z rówieśnikami, jak i z najbliższą rodziną. To także historia poszukiwania ojca, którego Łukasz nigdy nie poznał, a za którym tęsknił przez całe swoje dwunastoletnie życie.&quot;<\/span>\n  <a data-text-id=\"14858806958596903226\" href=\"#\" Reading in Patton’s Journal of Secrets, Kendra learns the location of the key to a vault housing one of the artifacts. In order to retrieve it, the Knights of the Dawn must enter a death trap — a dragon sanctuary called Wyrmroost. The mission cannot proceed without stealing a sacred object zealously guarded by the centaurs. Anybody seen Seth?\n\nThe race is on to acquire all five of the artifact keys to the great demon prison. Will the Knights of the Dawn conquer Wyrmroost? Who can stop the Sphinx? Can Vanessa be trusted to help? What artifact will be found next?<\/span>\n  <a data-text-id=\"17703976972160676741\" href=\"#\" onclick=\"swapContent(\$(this));; return false;\">...more<\/a>\n\n    <\/div>\n\n      <div This partial loads on almost every page view.  The associated React component makes
a call to SignInPromptController#get to determine if the user should see the sign in interstial.
This is determined by how many signed out pagehits the user has executed an how recently they have
last seen the insterstitial.  If the controller responds indicating the popup should appear, the
